### Post by Vorian on 2007-08-01
August 2007 Desktops - Posting Guidelines

* Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.

* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.

* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.

* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.

* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.

* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.

**[COLOR=DarkRed]*To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request  that you format your posts in the following order:[/COLOR]**

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

---

### Post by walkerk on 2007-08-01
> **ezphilosophy said:**
> I really like your AWN bar config!  Could you give me the details?  Color #?  Other details?

**Task Appearance:**

*Text:*
Color: #32424F (Opacity 255)
Shadow: Transparent
Background: Transparent
Font size: 12

*Arrows:*
Color: #1E343F (Opactity 153)


**Bar Appearance:**

*Borders*
Main Border: #151515 (Opactiy 34)
Internal border: Transparent

*Seperator:*
Show
Color: Transparent


**Glass Engine**

*Gradient*
First step color: #FFFFFF (Opacity 255)
Second step color: #191919 (Opacity 55

*Highlight*
First step color: Transparent
Second step color: Transparent

and of course in gconf-editor, under /apps/avant-window-navigator/bar: icon_offset = 18, bar_angle = 50.

### Post by urukrama on 2007-08-02
> **el mariachi said:**
> See docker? It has one "square" too many, that keeps disappearing and re-appearing -can't it be quiet? *I also need to find out how to move it and change it's color*

I'm not sure why the empty square is there. Does it appear when you start a particular app? To move docker, use obconf (on the Dock tab); since docker is a dockapp, it will move to wherever you place your dock. To change its colours, select a different theme. All dockapp background colours are controlled by your theme. If you just want to change the colour of your dock, but do not want to change theme, you can change the dock colour by changing the 'OSD' settings in the themerc file of your theme (normally ~/.themes/THEMENAME/openbox2/themerc). Note that this will also change your 'on screen display' colours (alt-tab, change desktops).

> Any ideas for Icons?

I would go for a icon theme with a darker touch, that matches the colours of your wallpaper and openbox/gtk theme. Some darker icon themes I have used in the past: whatever2, GnomeCorsair, Human Ultra Black/Gray, etc. Have a look at gnome-look.org

---

### Post by arbulus on 2007-08-02

how did you remove the window border from your termnial?

---

### Post by ayoli on 2007-08-02
> **arbulus said:**
> how did you remove the window border from your termnial?

with compiz-config manager, select windows decoration plugin and put somethiing like this in the line 'decoration windows':
```
(any & !(name=gnome-terminal | name=gkrellm)
```
that means every windows are decorated but gnome-terminal and gkrellm.
you need also regex matching compiz fusion plugin to be enabled.

---

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-08-03
@ el mariachi - I was wondering if you have tried to enable smooth fonts?

---

### Post by el mariachi on 2007-08-03
no, I didn't, or at least I don't remember doing it. The font rendering is set to "Best Contrast".
Do you think I should?

---

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-08-03
> **el mariachi said:**
> no, I didn't, or at least I don't remember doing it. The font rendering is set to "Best Contrast".
Do you think I should?

Try this, copy this code and save it as .fonts.conf in your ~/ folder.

```

<?xml version="1.0" ?>
<!DOCTYPE fontconfig SYSTEM "fonts.dtd">
<fontconfig>
<match target="font">
<edit name="autohint" mode="assign">
<bool>true</bool>
</edit>
</match>
</fontconfig>

```

You might want to enable your "anti-aliasing" for fonts, as well as your "hinting" and "sub-pixel hinting".

---

### Post by el mariachi on 2007-08-03
done that. I notice some differences in epiphany but none in thunar (for eg)
I have a CRT monitor, won't subpixel be worse for me?

---

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-08-03
> **el mariachi said:**
> done that. I notice some differences in epiphany but none in thunar (for eg)
I have a CRT monitor, won't subpixel be worse for me?

Check out your notepad where you wrote your untitled text file. It should give smooth fonts to your mousepad/notepad app.

As for your monitor, I'm not sure.

---

### Post by el mariachi on 2007-08-03
Yeah, it did! Thanks, I hadn't opened mousepad too check it out.

---

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-08-03
> **el mariachi said:**
> Yeah, it did! Thanks, I hadn't opened mousepad too check it out.

Yeah, it makes a big difference with the mousepad...and for me, the "Use anti-aliasing for fonts" and "Use hinting" really help my browser fonts...like the menubar fonts for File, Edit, View,....

---

@vexorian
_**I fixed the problem with the work spaces by using devilspie**_

the content of the file should be as follows

(if (is (application_name) "simdock") (begin skip_tasklist skip_pager pin below))
 
-------------------------------------------------------------------
add 
devilspie -a 
entry to startup

### Post by _simon_ on 2007-08-05
> **shearn89 said:**

Here's my new one - found a cool background (i think deviantart, but not sure - i'll post if anyone wants it.), and changed my pypanel launcher icons to an XFCE panel.

It's an addon called Stylish - [https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/2108](https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/2108)

And then the google theme is - [http://userstyles.org/styles/843](http://userstyles.org/styles/843)

If all you use is search and don't fancy messing around then you could use [http://www.blackle.com](http://www.blackle.com) or [http://www.black-google.blogspot.com/](http://www.black-google.blogspot.com/) (you can adblock the top bar)

### Post by Nekiruhs on 2007-08-05
> **el mariachi said:**
> where did you get the icons? they're areao right? i can't find them anywhereThe author of the icons requested them to be taken down, as they were ported without his/her knowledge or consent. But you can find them in [NovaLines]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/NovaLines?content=62546")
. Open the Tar.Gz and look inside, you will find 60500-areo-linux1.9fixed.tar.gz. Install it like a normal Icon theme.

### Post by PrimoTurbo on 2007-08-05

In photoshop 7 you make a new file, say 10by10 pixels then you draw a line from 1 corner to another. Then set it as a pattern and fill the picture u want the pattern.

### Post by dbbolton on 2007-08-06
> **orbital said:**
> How do you get AWN to look 3D like that, with the reflections?
open gconf and navigate to /apps/avant-window-navigator/bar and change bar_angle to 45 and icon_offset to 18.

### Post by 4KvRMU7Nnv on 2007-08-08
[[IMG]http://img471.imageshack.us/img471/605/screenshotgy0.png[/IMG]](http://imageshack.us)

Standard Ubuntu look...I did change it slightly...

Metacity:  Human-squared
Gtk2: Murrina Human Classic (slighty modified with Murrine configurator)
Icons: Human

The above information is not as important as the applications I'm running:

The sphere is drawn with an EXCELLENT mathematics program called Mathematica.  It can do pretty much everything.  [not opensource]

While not running, my movie player is also amazing.  SMplayer.  So far it can play every video type I have thrown at it perfectly. [opensource]

Audacity [beta version] recording software that is very intuitive.  Much easier than Ardour which is very confusing.  Also, the beta version has Gtk2 support so you don't have to work in the old gtk1 interface.  Havn't encountered any errors in the development version either.  had to compile it myself.

The cow that displays my message is drawn by a cute little simple program called "cowsay."  It's in the repository. 


I'm disappointed in the fixation on GUI as opposed to the programs one uses which, in the end is what is truly important.  Not enough of either is bad!


EDIT:: 
the theme in Mathematica is not the theme in the rest of the computer.  It uses the QT engine so it had to look that way.  Nevertheless...the output of Mathematica is stunning!

---

### Post by Tyche on 2007-08-10
Theme is the simple ClearLooks (blue)
The background is what is important:

Using the SCOsinks.jpg created by J.D. "Illiad" Frazer of "UserFriendly" fame.  The cartoon depicts Pamela Jones in the foreground with The SCO Group ship sinking in the background.

The news just came in to Groklaw ([http://www.groklaw.net/article.php?story=20070810165237718](http://www.groklaw.net/article.php?story=20070810165237718)) that Judge Kimbal has ruled AGAINST The SCO Group (Caldera) owning any UNIX copyrights.  This pretty much guts their cases against both Novell and IBM.

### Post by kvonb on 2007-08-11
Here is the latest addition to my ever growing Ubuntu family of systems :).

I finally scored a laptop quite cheap off ebay, it's an Acer Travelmate 240, Celeron 2.4/512 RAM/20 gig hdd.

It has an Intel 855 GME video card (16meg shared) and the screen is limited to 1024x768, but everything works beautifully with Feisty, even Beryl/Compiz with no messing around :).

Theme details, all installed using the Gnome Art Manager:

Window border - Graphite
Icons - NuoveXT 2.1

### Post by el mariachi on 2007-08-11
Just a minor update.

I've found an easy and stupidly obvious way of using tint without having it above maximized windows: Openbox's margins. I just made the bottom margin the same size as tint (25px for me) and now it rocks :D

---

### Post by marco123 on 2007-08-11
Wanted to try a Hacker style theme again. :)

Controls - Smoked glass, Gnome-Look.
Window border - ATER-Blue, Gnome-Look.
Icons - Linsta, Gnome-Look.
Wallpaper - Eminating Energy, Deviantart.
Conky + Transparent Eterm.

For Eterm input : "Eterm --trans -g 90x20+0+40 -L 10000 -b black -f  white --shade 0 -x --borderless --scrollbar 0 --buttonbar 0 -c grey89 &"
 and you will have  transparent terminal built into desktop. :)

Shot at 2007-08-11

### Post by tbroderick on 2007-08-11
[[IMG]http://img441.imageshack.us/img441/9012/200708111723341280x1024bn1.th.png[/IMG]](http://img441.imageshack.us/my.php?image=200708111723341280x1024bn1.png)
[URL="http://dwm.suckless.org/"]
dwm[/URL], [urxvt]("http://software.schmorp.de/pkg/rxvt-unicode.html"), [mutt]("http://www.mutt.org/"), [newsneuter]("http://synflood.at/newsbeuter.html"), and [gtk2_prefs]("http://members.lycos.co.uk/alexv6/") shown.

**dwm colors**
#define NORMBORDERCOLOR         "#3d3c3a"
#define NORMBGCOLOR                "#92aeb7"
#define NORMFGCOLOR             "#222222"
#define SELBORDERCOLOR          "#92aeb7"
#define SELBGCOLOR              "#3e3c3a"
#define SELFGCOLOR              "#92aeb7"

**gtk2 theme**
[GSM]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/GSM+GTK?content=56104")

**fonts**
[proggyclean]("http://www.proggyfonts.com/index.php?menu=download") for terminal and dwm
dejavu sans for gtk2

**Misc**
[Xdefaults]("http://pastebin.com/f43aa6f9d")

### Post by dbbolton on 2007-08-12
> **luckyd said:**
> has anyone had problems with conky and compiz-fusion. Like the backround being black?
that's probably because you're probably using nautilus so you have to have "own_window yes". so compiz treats conky like a window. there is a "window color" option in the ~/.conkyrc file but i don't think you can make it transparent and add composite effects. this thread might be of more help:
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=281865](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=281865)

---

I've attached my conky, it's actually 7 conky scripts that are all started by "dual-conky" (edit the paths accordingly). The Gmail.py template can be found here: [http://vredfreak.atspace.com/projects.html](http://vredfreak.atspace.com/projects.html)

As for conky appearing on both the left and right side, do you mean on both monitors or on each side of one screen? You can easily put conky's anywhere by messing with this section:

```
alignment bottom_right
gap_x 0
gap_y 0
```

You make one of them bottom_left, the other bottom_right, etc. and they appear accordingly.

@shearn: The font is Telegraphem, it's from [http://www.dafont.com](http://www.dafont.com).

---

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-08-12
Check out my new Gmail skin...using the Firefox extension "Stylish", I was able to take 3 different scripts, and change all the colors and some pixel sizes, and perfectly match my gtk-2.0 theme.


Large 1280x800 view: [http://i144.photobucket.com/albums/r161/crimesaucer/Screenshot-20-16.png](http://i144.photobucket.com/albums/r161/crimesaucer/Screenshot-20-16.png)
[IMG]http://i144.photobucket.com/albums/r161/crimesaucer/Screenshot-20-17.png[/IMG]


Here are the 3 Stylish scripts that work to create this:
[http://userstyles.org/styles/3065](http://userstyles.org/styles/3065)
[http://userstyles.org/styles/1483](http://userstyles.org/styles/1483)
[http://userstyles.org/styles/1916](http://userstyles.org/styles/1916)


...then click advanced on each script and adjust the hex color codes to match your theme. It takes a little while to figure out what color affects what part, but it's worth it.

---

### Post by smartboyathome on 2007-08-14
NEW SCREENSHOTS!!!

The first one is how my desktop looks normally (panels are autohidden, GIMPed out the icons on the desktop). The second shows my panels (GIMPed in the bottom panel and out the icons on the desktop). The third one shows my metacity, GTK, and other info (NOTE! the wallpaper isn't correct on that yet). I am currently in the process of creating a new look for salocin, but my wallpaper is an edited version of [this wallpaper.]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Waterfire?content=61428") My icons are an edited version of [this icon set]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Glass+Icons+Theme?content=32146"). ### Post by Chaotic Thought on 2007-08-15
**Window Maker in harmony with GNOME**

This is my current Ubuntu 7.04 desktop, attempting to run Window Maker smoothly with the standard Ubuntu-packaged GNOME (including the desktop icons). I used gnome-color-chooser to change the color of the panels to better match the Window Maker icon tiles, and then positioned the top GNOME panel appropriately to fit with the Window Maker docks. Also, I deleted the "window list" panel that's normally at the bottom of the screen. With the Window Maker dock, you can click the application icons to raise or iconify their windows.

**Themes**:
Window decorations: Standard Window Maker gradient theme, with customized colors
GTK2: Murrina Simpleblue theme (from gnome-look.org), 

**Wallpaper**: "Opera in space" from the unofficial Opera wallpaper forum: [http://my.opera.com/community/forums/topic.dml?id=47601&page=2#comment730393](http://my.opera.com/community/forums/topic.dml?id=47601&page=2#comment730393)

**Programs**:
Window manager: Window Maker 0.92
Panels: GNOME (**gnome-panel**), XFCE 4.4.0 (**xfce4-panel**)
Desktop: GNOME (**nautilus**), adesklets ("Weatherforecast.py"), gdesklets ("Disk space monitor"), and **gdeskcal**.
Dockapps: **wmmemfree** (1st and 2nd screens, right middle), **wmfire** (2nd screen, top right)

[[IMG]http://img361.imageshack.us/img361/5005/wmdesktop200708eq6.th.png[/IMG]]("http://img361.imageshack.us/img361/5005/wmdesktop200708eq6.png")
**Initial Desktop**

[[IMG]http://img377.imageshack.us/img377/229/wmwindows200708jo3.th.png[/IMG]]("http://img377.imageshack.us/img377/229/wmwindows200708jo3.png")
**Desktop with some open windows**

[[IMG]http://img369.imageshack.us/img369/879/wmminimal200708ol4.th.png[/IMG]]("http://img369.imageshack.us/img369/879/wmminimal200708ol4.png")
**Minimal Mode** (panels and desktop icons hidden in the dock)

### Post by Chaotic Thought on 2007-08-15
> **BOBSONATOR said:**
> 
How do you dudes/dudeettes like this one?

Its basically full on Mire from gnome-look.

Oh, wow... that's an extremely nice, dark themed desktop. Please give us some hints as to which themes you used.

I've gotta say, I absolutely love the idea of dark themes--they're a lot better on the eyes, and I think computer screens are *meant* to display bright text on a dark background. (Think about the computer systems in science fiction television/movies, and you'll be hard pressed to find a fictional system of the future with Mac OS-style black text on a bright background).

However--I'm always afraid to make my desktop dark, because it seems to work well with certain applications but clash terribly with others. In today's current computer world, it seems like all Web and application developers assume the user has a bright background with black text. For example, try opening a web browser, and the dark theme will probably not stand so well against most of the web sites out there (including this one).

Anyway, it looks very cool in your shots, if you post some more you might convince me to try dark themes again. --- (And a P.S. about the Web sites clashing with dark themes... as I recall, there is a Firefox plugin on mozilla.org that lets you deal with web sites to force them to fit dark themes better, but as with many things, it requires some tweaking. And alas, some sites simply can't be dealt with because they have hardcoded colors instead of style sheets, or they're using images with white backgrounds instead of transparency)

---

### Post by PrimoTurbo on 2007-08-15
I switched to xubuntu for a little while, to be honest however I have been using XP for the last 2 weeks because I have been playing al ot of Warcraft 3 DOTA.

It's pretty boring in general, 1 thing that is interesting is the fact that I have found a way to get rid of the borders around icon names.

[[IMG]http://img355.imageshack.us/img355/6793/aug152007xu0.th.png[/IMG]](http://img355.imageshack.us/my.php?image=aug152007xu0.png)

Basically all you need to do is edit ~/.gtkrc-2.0 and add the following:


```
style "xfdesktop-icon-view" {
    XfdesktopIconView::label-alpha = 0

    base[NORMAL] = "#3F6BA4"
    base[SELECTED] = "#3F6BA4"
    base[ACTIVE] = "#3F6BA4"

    fg[NORMAL] = "#ffffff"
    fg[SELECTED] = "#ffffff"
    fg[ACTIVE] = "#ffffff"
}
widget_class "*XfdesktopIconView*" style "xfdesktop-icon-view"
```

XfdesktopIconView::label-alpha = 0 determines the alpha level of the desktop label.

For some reasons xubuntu seems a little delayed like when I type, I notice there are slow downs every now and then....Gnome doesn't have these problems, going to KDE for a little while anyways.

---

### Post by mushroom on 2007-08-17
[http://i13.tinypic.com/625xea1.jpg](http://i13.tinypic.com/625xea1.jpg)

I heart evilwm. It's essentially bare X with moving, resizing, closing, maximizing, virtual desktops and the ability to launch an xterm, all with hotkeys and one pixel window borders to indicate focus. After switching between KDE, Gnome and XFCE for a year or so I delved into minimalism for a bit, and finally found the perfect window manager. No desktop widgets, menus or any dreaded "file managers"; just start up, open an xterm and away I go :D

### Post by What is in a name? on 2007-08-17
> **fuscia said:**
> a true sign of sanity. i really like how you matched your wallpaper to the theme.

Thanks a lot, Fuscia!... You wouldn't believe all the time I spent looking for something that would really satisfy my taste and leave me inspired to work. And after several attempts, I believe that once I again I had the proof that urban wallpapers work best with me... And I love the fact that I can do everything I want with the menu. I'm using  Obmenu to configure it, and now I distributed my apps according to particular categories related to verbs. Office and image editing programs are in CREATE; messengers and mail clients are in COMMUNICATE; media players are in ENJOY; games are in PLAY... And so on. I'm still perfecting it, though...

> **dbbolton said:**
> why, that's a lovely openbox theme you've got there ;)

Actually, I saw the Bamboo Openbox theme in a desktop screenshot from the last month (I think) combined with Murrina Brown, which I tried to reproduce in my own PC... However, it didn't completely please me, so I made some more experiences, and finally went with Murrina Relax, which is one of my favourites. Though I got a bit tired of it when I was in GNOME, now I saw a new opportunity for it when I came across Bamboo. I really love warm colours (particularly red and orange, mixed with brown and black tones).

> **el mariachi said:**
> Will you release it as a compilation? They fit really well together!
(btw: Português?:KS)

I still don't have it all completed,  BUT most of the job is done... It is a work in progress. So, yes, good idea. I will try to compilate it in an archive and release it in Gnome-Look or something similar. Thanks for the compliments!

P.S.: Sim, sou português!... Hehe... É um prazer encontrar um luso por estas bandas!!

Openbox rocks its socks!

Professional Architect #22.

### Post by Miguel on 2007-08-18
> **urukrama said:**
> I didn't even know there was a version 2.

It was released only recently. Version 2.0 included some nice changes (no more white firefox) plus some nasty regressions, including (IMHO) too light folders, impersonal arrows and an out of line help icon. This is curious since nuoveXT-1.6 folders were some of the best out there. I found them much nicer than OS X folder icons, and probably on par with Vista*. There have been two subsecuent releases, and version 2.2 is pretty nice, although I don't like the ssh emblems. 

I'm attaching two screenshots for the sake of comparison. Excuse the compression artifacts. I hope the names are kept in a straightforward fashion.

*As much as I despise Vista's theme for blurred window borders and little differenciation between focused and unfocused windows, I find their icon theme exquisite.

*EDIT:* It's 1.6 on the left and 2.2 on the right. As a sidenote, both versions are available in the [author's site](http://nuovext.pwsp.net/)

*EDIT 2:* Yes, I'm an icon freak. But I suspect I'm not the only one in this thread.

### Post by el mariachi on 2007-08-19
> **What is in a name? said:**
> If only it was possible to present open applications of all workspaces on TTM, I would ditch Visibility permanently... I really could use some more help on this.
You already have an app that does that:D pypanel!
You just need to edit this line in ~/.pypanelrc
```
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Show All Applications: Show apps from all desktops or just the current
# 0: Disabled - Only applications on the current desktop will be displayed
# 1: Enabled  - Selected apps are moved to the current desktop
# 2: Enabled  - Current desktop is changed to the selected apps desktop
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHOWALL         = 0             # 0, 1 or 2 - see descriptions above

```Just change it to 1 or 2 :KS

EDIT: If you do this TTM will lose it's purpose (I don't know if TTM can be configured to do the same)

---

### Post by urukrama on 2007-08-19
> **What is in a name? said:**
> However, here at OB, I'm totally for text and no icons over the wallpaper. So, I'm in a dillema. If only it was possible to present open applications of all workspaces on TTM, I would ditch Visibility permanently... I really could use some more help on this.

Why don't you use Pypanel's task list? It can show windows from all desktops, and you can disable window icons (and have only text). If you play around with the colours and transparency a bit, you can get something that looks quite nice. If you want to have a tint-like look, you can play with the vertical lines (which will show between each item on your task list), by giving them the colour of your wallpaper. Have a look at the .pypanelrc file in your home directory.

Or you can just forget about the whole thing. Do you really need a task list? I've been using Openbox without a panel or task list for a while now. It takes some getting used to, but once you're settled in a panel-free environment, you'll have a hard time moving back to a panel :-) I use the alt-tab dialog to switch between windows, or sometimes even [skippy]("http://thegraveyard.org/skippy.php") (in the repos).

---

### Post by s_spiff on 2007-08-20
> **el mariachi said:**
> You already have an app that does that:D pypanel!
You just need to edit this line in ~/.pypanelrc
```
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Show All Applications: Show apps from all desktops or just the current
# 0: Disabled - Only applications on the current desktop will be displayed
# 1: Enabled  - Selected apps are moved to the current desktop
# 2: Enabled  - Current desktop is changed to the selected apps desktop
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHOWALL         = 0             # 0, 1 or 2 - see descriptions above

```Just change it to 1 or 2 :KS

EDIT: If you do this TTM will lose it's purpose (I don't know if TTM can be configured to do the same)

Can something like this be done for the default gnome panel? I have beryl installed, but now when I do a Ctrl+Alt+Left or Right I don't switch to a different workspace. I deleted the original panel that came with a fresh install. Anyway to get it back with original cofig?

### Post by urukrama on 2007-08-20
> **s_spiff said:**
> Can something like this be done for the default gnome panel? I have beryl installed, but now when I do a Ctrl+Alt+Left or Right I don't switch to a different workspace. I deleted the original panel that came with a fresh install. Anyway to get it back with original cofig?

Yes. Right click on the task list, select Preferences, and then tick 'Show windows from all workspaces' (on the Behaviour tab). The gnome-panel task list applet is independent from Metacity, so it will work no matter what window manager you use.

---

### Post by BobCFC on 2007-08-21
> **smartboyathome said:**
> I would suggest reading up on XML before you get too far into theming. That is the language that GNOME uses. Then try the tutorials.

btw, what do you like about that theme? I am always looking to improve mine ;)


I just like the small white on black min/max/close controls in the title bar. I also quite like the shiny black glass buttons he stole from Kore but I don't think they would go with your slate grey GTK.  While I don't like his pure black GTK it does make your grey Metacity border stand out nicely even though he didn't change it.

If I were to do a dark theme I would change the white text input fields to grey as well.  I read a comment on another dark theme which said the trick was 'not to let any light escape' because dark themes are easier on the eyes at night.  I can't remember where I read that but [this theme]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/show.php?content=58118") seems to have the same philosophy.


Thanks... XML is just a fancy datastructure to us C++ guys... I wrote my own parser a few years ago lol.

---

### Post by BobCFC on 2007-08-21
> **s_spiff said:**
> Fabulous!!! thanks you so much. Now only if someone could tell me how to get beryl/gnome to allow me to put different wall papers on different workspaces!

You need compiz to do this properly.  There was a port of the wallpaper plugin to Beryl but it was just a hack and meant that you lost your desktop icons.

As a fellow Beryl fan I can say Compiz Fusion is worth the jump for the reflections and the dodge plugin anyway.  Beryl will not be developed further.


EDIT: Compiz Fusion is installed by default in the next version of Ubuntu anyway, called Gutsy Gibbon 7.10 out in October.

### Post by Pepsta on 2007-08-22
> **Dark Star said:**
> Awesome cube .. Now can u tell me how to change the background of the surrounding of the cuube .. Thank sS:D

You will have to add a "Skydome" image, under Compiz it can be found at **System - Preferences - CompizConfig Setting Manager - Desktop Cube - Appearance**

Hope this helps.

---

### Post by misfitpierce on 2007-08-22
> **Pepsta said:**
> You will have to add a "Skydome" image, under Compiz it can be found at **System - Preferences - CompizConfig Setting Manager - Desktop Cube - Appearance**

Hope this helps.

While we on subject do you by chance have compiz repoo with newest compiz fusion release?

---

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-08-22
> **Dark Star said:**
> Awesome cube .. Now can u tell me how to change the background of the surrounding of the cuube .. Thank sS:D

Like Pepsta said, you need to have a Skydome image.

Your Skydome image must be either 2:1 ratio size or 4:1

My Skydome is 2048 pixels wide and 1024 pixels in height (2048x1024).


You will also need to enable Cube Reflection for that mirror effect.

---

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-08-22
> **misfitpierce said:**
> While we on subject do you by chance have compiz repoo with newest compiz fusion release?

EDIT: (I misread your question)

Yes, I use Compiz Fusion with Trevino's Eye Candy Repository. I also use the unofficial plug-ins.

I still can't understand how dwm works.. guess I'll really have to try it.

---

### Post by finferflu on 2007-08-28
> **el mariachi said:**
> I still can't understand how dwm works.. guess I'll really have to try it.
The concept is quite simple: you have 2 modes, tiled and floating. The latter is the one most WMs use, the former is specific to dwm. In tiling mode the desktop is divided into 2 areas, the main area and the tiled area. In the main area the window occupies the whole length of the screen vertically, whereas in the tiled area you have all the other windows sharing the vertical space (every window having equal size). Obviously you can switch between windows to decide which one is gonna occupy the main area, and you can also resize the main area. It's like having minimized windows on which you can actually work. Everything can be done with the keyboard, mouse is only optional :)
Finally you have tags instead of workspaces, and you can apply multiple tags on every window, so you can bind a window to workspaces 1, 4, and 7, instead than the classical sticky mode that binds it to all workspaces.

---

### Post by Interestedinthepenguin on 2007-08-29
@BoyOfDestiny:  Nice theme.  Care to share/upload it?

---

### Post by BoyOfDestiny on 2007-08-29
> **Interestedinthepenguin said:**
> @BoyOfDestiny:  Nice theme.  Care to share/upload it?

Thanks.

I'm using Gutsy alpha, so there is a nice tool to let you tweak the colors (of themes that support it)

There is a file, in ~/.themes/SafariCherryDark/index.theme

The folder name being what I named saved the theme as

The contents are here:
```
[Desktop Entry]
Name=SafariCherryDark
Type=X-GNOME-Metatheme
Comment=
Encoding=UTF-8

[X-GNOME-Metatheme]
GtkTheme=Darklooks
MetacityTheme=Clearlooks
IconTheme=gartoon
GtkColorScheme=fg_color:#a8a8a8a8a8a8,bg_color:#300030004000,text_color:#b5b5b2$
CursorTheme=default
CursorSize=32

```

So it's not a .gtkrc file to share...

Hopefully that works, I'll attach the file and a screenshot with the colors shown.

EDIT: Darklooks itself is in the package gnome-themes-extras
